  Files created

  File: auth/AuthContext.jsx
  Purpose: createContext(null) only — the context object in its own file so the
    provider and the hook both import it with no circular dependency. Default
    null lets the hook detect misuse.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: auth/AuthProvider.jsx
  Purpose: Holds the auth state. token state is initialized from localStorage
    (getToken()) so a refresh keeps you signed in. Exposes a memoized value: { 
    token, isAuthenticated, login(token), logout() }. login persists the token +

    updates state; logout clears both.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: hooks/useAuth.js
  Purpose: useAuth() — reads the context via useContext, throws a clear error if

    used outside <AuthProvider>. The single API every component uses for auth.

  Files updated

  - auth/ProtectedRoute.jsx — now reads isAuthenticated from useAuth() instead
  of calling authStorage directly. Token present → <Outlet/>; absent → <Navigate
  to="/login" replace/>.
  - components/Layout.jsx — logout now calls useAuth().logout() (updates context
  state, so the guard re-renders and redirects) instead of clearing storage
  directly.
  - main.jsx — wrapped <App/> in <AuthProvider> (inside <BrowserRouter>), so the
  whole tree can consume auth.

  localStorage remains the JWT store (via the existing auth/authStorage.js
  helpers, now used only by AuthProvider — components go through context, not
  storage).

  Flow: Login → Context → ProtectedRoute

  ┌─ Login (future API step) ─────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ LoginPage submit → useAuth().login(token)                         │
  │   → authStorage.setToken(token)   // localStorage write           │
  │   → setTokenState(token)          // React state update           │
  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                            │  context value changes
                            ▼
  ┌─ AuthContext (AuthProvider) ──────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ value = { token, isAuthenticated: Boolean(token), login, logout } │
  │ re-renders all consumers                                          │
  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                            │  useAuth()
                            ▼
  ┌─ ProtectedRoute ──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ isAuthenticated ? <Outlet/> (render /dashboard)                   │
  │                 : <Navigate to="/login" replace/>                 │
  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  1. Login (wired in the next step) will hand the API's JWT to login(token).
  Right now no backend is called, so no token is produced.
  2. Context persists the token to localStorage and flips isAuthenticated to
  true, re-rendering consumers.
  3. ProtectedRoute reads the new value via useAuth() and renders the protected
  Layout/DashboardPage; Logout runs the reverse — logout() clears the token,
  isAuthenticated becomes false, and the guard redirects to /login.
  4. On refresh, AuthProvider re-seeds token from localStorage, so a logged-in
  user stays in.

  Current behavior unchanged for preview: with no token, /dashboard redirects to
  /login. To preview while the login API is still pending, set
  localStorage.setItem('tms.auth.token','dev') and reload (the provider reads it
  on mount); logout clears it.

  Next step is wiring the Axios client + LoginPage → login() against POST 
  /api/auth/login. Say the word and I'll implement the API layer.

  Files created

  File: api/axiosClient.js
  Purpose: Pre-configured Axios instance (base URL + JSON header) with request
    and response interceptors. The single client every API module uses.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: api/authApi.js
  Purpose: login({ username, password }) → POST /auth/login, returns the
    ApiResponse<LoginResponseDto> envelope.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: api/taskApi.js
  Purpose: getTasks(filter), getTaskById(id), createTask(payload),
  updateTask(id,
     payload), deleteTask(id), getTaskSummary() — one function per backend
    endpoint, each returning the ApiResponse<T> envelope.

  Also updated: .env.development → VITE_API_BASE_URL=http://localhost:5210/api
  (matches requirement #2; the client reads the env var and falls back to that
  exact URL).

  Configuration details

  - Base URL resolves from import.meta.env.VITE_API_BASE_URL with a hardcoded
  fallback of http://localhost:5210/api. Production uses /api (nginx proxy) via
  .env.production.
  - Token source = localStorage through the existing authStorage helpers — no
  duplication.
  - Login exemption: the 401 handler skips the global redirect when the failing
  request is /auth/login, so bad-credential errors surface to the (future) login
  page instead of bouncing the user.

  Interceptor flow

  Request interceptor (outgoing):
  component → authApi/taskApi → axiosClient.request
     → [request interceptor] read token from localStorage
         token? → set  Authorization: Bearer <token>
     → request sent to http://localhost:5210/api/...
  Every protected call automatically carries the JWT — callers never set the
  header themselves.

  Response interceptor (incoming):
  API response → [response interceptor]
     ├─ 2xx success → pass through unchanged → caller gets response.data
  (ApiResponse)
     └─ error:
          status === 401  AND  not the /auth/login call ?
              → clearToken()                       (drop the dead/expired JWT)
              → if not already on /login:
                    window.location.assign('/login')   (global redirect)
          → Promise.reject(error)  → caller's catch still runs

  So an expired or invalid token on any protected request triggers one global
  reaction — purge the token and redirect to /login — instead of each page
  handling auth expiry on its own. The Promise.reject is preserved so
  component-level try/catch (e.g. showing an error toast) still works for
  non-401 errors.

  ▎ Note: the 401 redirect uses window.location.assign (a full navigation) 
  ▎ because interceptors live outside React Router and have no access to 
  ▎ navigate(). This reliably resets app state on forced logout.

  Not touched (as instructed)

  LoginPage and DashboardPage are unchanged — no API calls wired into components
  yet. The next step would connect LoginPage.handleSubmit → authApi.login() →
  useAuth().login(token), and DashboardPage → taskApi.getTasks().

● Builds clean — 89 modules now (axios is bundled in via LoginPage → authApi → 
  axiosClient, confirming the API layer is actually wired in).

  What was implemented

  LoginPage.jsx (integrated):
  - Calls authApi.login({ username, password }) on submit.
  - On success: pulls { token, username } from response.data, calls
  useAuth().login(token, username), and navigate('/dashboard', { replace: true 
  }).
  - Loading state: loading flag disables both inputs and the button; button text
  switches to "Signing in…".
  - Error display: a general message banner from apiResponse.message, plus a
  bulleted list of apiResponse.errors (the FluentValidation messages) when
  present; a network-failure fallback when there's no response.

  Supporting changes:
  - AuthProvider / authStorage / constants — now also persist and expose
  username (STORAGE_KEYS.USERNAME), so context carries { token, username, 
  isAuthenticated, login, logout }. login(token, username) and logout() keep
  both in sync.
  - Layout — header shows "Signed in as {username}" using the stored value.
  - index.css — added alert and disabled-button styles.

  Login flow, end-to-end

  1. User types username/password → submits the form
          │
  2. LoginPage.handleSubmit()
          │  setLoading(true); clear previous errors
          ▼
  3. authApi.login({ username, password })
          │  POST http://localhost:5210/api/auth/login
          │  (axios request interceptor runs, but no token yet → no auth header)
          ▼
  4. Backend AuthController → AuthService
          ├─ valid  → 200 { success:true, data:{ token, username, role,
  expiresAt } }
          ├─ bad creds → 401 { success:false, message:"Invalid username or
  password." }
          └─ empty fields → 400 { success:false, message:"Validation failed.",
  errors:[...] }
          │
  5a. SUCCESS (2xx):
          │  response.data → { token, username, ... }
          │  useAuth().login(token, username)
          │      → authStorage.setToken / setUsername   (localStorage)
          │      → AuthContext state updates → isAuthenticated = true
          │  navigate('/dashboard', { replace:true })
          ▼
  6.  ProtectedRoute re-reads context → isAuthenticated true → renders
  <Layout><DashboardPage/>
          (Layout header now shows "Signed in as <username>")

  5b. FAILURE (400/401 → axios throws):
          │  caught in handleSubmit
          │  error.response.data = ApiResponse envelope
          │  setErrorMessage(message) + setFieldErrors(errors[])
          │  (response interceptor skips its global 401 redirect for
  /auth/login,
          │   so the error stays on the login page)
          ▼
     Error banner renders; user stays on /login

  Always: finally → setLoading(false)

  The key handoff is step 5a: API → AuthContext → ProtectedRoute. Storing the
  token via context (not directly) is what makes isAuthenticated flip and the
  guard let the user through — and a later expired token on any protected call
  triggers the interceptor's global 401 → clear token → redirect back to /login.

  Verifying it

  The backend login contract was already proven in the smoke test. To exercise
  the full UI flow: start the API (dotnet run --project src/TMS.API, port 5210)
  and the SPA (cd frontend; npm run dev), then log in with admin / Admin@123 →
  you'll land on the dashboard; a wrong password shows the "Invalid username or
  password." banner; empty fields show the validation list. Want me to run that
  end-to-end check, or move on to the dashboard task list / API integration?

  Access-Control-Allow-Origin, so the browser allows the cross-origin POST.
  Bearer-token auth doesn't need cookies, so AllowCredentials isn't required.

  │                              │ Renders the task table (Title,            │

  │ pages/DashboardPage.jsx      │ Orchestrates the hook + components;       │
  │                              │ handles loading/error/refresh.            │
  └──────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Plus index.css additions (cards grid, table, badge colors, header).

  Component design (why it's structured this way)

  Layered, single-responsibility split:
  DashboardPage  ──uses──▶ useDashboardData ──calls──▶ taskApi ──▶ axiosClient
  ──▶ API
       │                        (data + state)
       ├── renders ▶ SummaryCards  (derives counts from summary.groups)
       └── renders ▶ TaskTable ──▶ StatusBadge / PriorityBadge

  - Data fetching lives in a hook, not the component. useDashboardData owns the
  network calls, loading/error state, and reload(). DashboardPage stays a thin
  orchestrator — easy to read and to test the hook independently.
  - Parallel load. Tasks and summary are independent, so Promise.all fetches
  both at once (one combined loading/error) instead of waterfalling.
  - Presentational components are dumb. SummaryCards, TaskTable, StatusBadge,
  PriorityBadge take props and render — no API knowledge, fully reusable (the
  badges will be reused in the create/edit views later).
  - Summary cards are derived, not stored. The backend returns grouped (status, 
  priority, count) rows. countByStatus sums them per status for To Do / In 
  Progress / Completed, while Total Tasks uses summary.total. This matches the
  grouped contract we locked earlier — no separate per-status endpoint needed.
  - Enum mapping centralized. Integers → labels (and CSS color classes) live in
  taskEnums.js, so a label change is one edit. Unknown values fall back to
  "Unknown" rather than rendering a raw number.
  - States handled explicitly: loading ("Loading dashboard…" + disabled
  Refresh), error (red alert from apiResponse.message), and the empty case ("No
  tasks found."). A 401 is handled globally by the axios interceptor (token
  cleared → redirect to /login), so the dashboard doesn't special-case auth
  expiry.

  To see it

  With the API running on :5210 (restarted with CORS) and npm run dev on :5173,
  log in as admin / Admin@123 → the dashboard shows 4 summary cards (Total 12,
  plus To Do / In Progress / Completed splits) and the seeded tasks in the
  table.

  Next logical steps: filters (status/priority → getTasks({ status, priority 
  })), and create/edit/delete task UI. Want me to take those on?

● Builds clean — 97 modules. Create Task is implemented against POST /api/tasks.

  Files

  File: components/TaskForm.jsx (new)
  Role: Controlled create form — title, description, priority (select),
    assignedTo. Owns its form state, validation, and submit. No status field
    (backend forces ToDo).
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: pages/DashboardPage.jsx (updated)
  Role: "New Task" toggle, renders TaskForm, refreshes list + summary on
  success,
    shows success banner.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  File: index.css
  Role: Form layout, success alert, field-error, textarea styles.

  Requirements coverage

  1. TaskForm component — created, reusable.
  2. Controlled components — every input is bound to form state via value + a
  shared handleChange (name/value), so React state is the single source of
  truth.
  3. Validation — client-side validate() mirrors backend rules (title required +
  ≤200, description ≤1000, assignedTo ≤100); per-field errors render inline. If
  the request still 400s, the backend's errors[]/message surface in the form's
  error banner — defense in depth.
  4. Refresh after create — onSuccess → parent's handleCreated calls reload(),
  re-fetching tasks and summary so the new row and updated counts appear.
  5. Success/error messages — green success banner on the dashboard (Task "X" 
  created.); red error banner inside the form for submit failures; inline field
  errors for validation.

  State management approach

  DashboardPage (owns: list/summary data via useDashboardData, showForm,
  successMessage)
     │  props: onSuccess(reload + banner), onCancel
     ▼
  TaskForm (owns: form fields, field errors, submitting, submitError)
     │  createTask(payload) → POST /api/tasks
     └─ success → onSuccess(createdTask) ──▶ parent reloads + shows banner

  - Local form state stays in TaskForm. Field values, validation errors, the
  submitting flag, and submitError are all useState inside the form — they're
  the form's private concern and don't belong in the parent. One form object
  with a generic handleChange keeps it concise and scalable.
  - Server state stays in the hook. The task list and summary live in
  useDashboardData. The form never touches that data directly — it just signals
  "I created something" via the onSuccess callback, and the parent re-fetches
  (server is the source of truth). This avoids optimistic-update bugs and
  guarantees the summary counts are accurate.
  - Communication is one-way via callbacks (onSuccess/onCancel) — child→parent.
  No shared mutable state, no context needed for this; the form is
  self-contained and could be dropped into an edit flow later.
  - Submission is guarded: submitting disables all inputs and the buttons
  (prevents double-submit), and validation short-circuits before any network
  call.

  This mirrors the dashboard's existing pattern: local UI/form state in 
  components, server state in hooks, refresh-on-mutation rather than client-side
  cache juggling.

  To try it: with API (:5210) + npm run dev (:5173) running and logged in as
  admin/Admin@123, click New Task, fill the form, Create Task → the form closes,
  a success banner shows, and the new task appears in the table with the counts
  updated.

  Next: edit/status-change, soft delete, and filters. Want those next?

  Requirements coverage

  1. Edit modal — EditTaskModal (form inside Modal), prefilled, includes
  Status/Priority selects + title/description/assignedTo.
  2. Delete confirmation — ConfirmDialog asks before deleting; notes it's a soft
  delete.
  3. Refresh after operations — both handleUpdated and confirmDelete call
  reload() (re-fetches tasks and summary).
  4. API errors handled — edit shows backend errors[]/message inside the modal;
  delete shows the error inside the confirm dialog (dialog stays open so the
  user can retry/cancel); a 401 still triggers the global interceptor redirect.

  Update (edit) flow

  Row "Edit" ──▶ onEdit(task) ──▶ DashboardPage: setEditingTask(task)
                                           │
                                           ▼
                            <EditTaskModal task=… />  (form state seeded from
  task)
                                           │  user edits, Save
                                           ▼
                            validate() ── invalid ─▶ inline field errors (no
  call)
                                           │ valid
                                           ▼
                            updateTask(id, payload)  ──▶ PUT /api/tasks/{id}
                                           │
                ┌──────────── success (2xx) ─────────────┐
                ▼                                          ▼  error (400/throw)
     onSuccess(updatedTask)                         submitError shown in modal
     → setEditingTask(null)  (close modal)          (modal stays open to retry)
     → success banner
     → reload()  ── re-fetch tasks + summary ──▶ table & counts reflect change

  Delete flow is the same shape: onDelete → setDeletingTask → ConfirmDialog →
  confirmDelete() calls deleteTask(id) (DELETE) → on success closes the dialog,
  shows the banner, and reload()s; the soft-deleted task disappears from the
  list and the summary counts drop (backend excludes IsDeleted).

  State design (consistent with the rest of the app):
  - Server state stays in useDashboardData; mutations never patch it locally —
  they call reload() so the list/summary always match the database (the
  soft-delete + grouped-summary semantics are honored automatically).
  - UI/modal state (editingTask, deletingTask, deleteLoading/Error) lives in
  DashboardPage; each modal owns its own form/submit state. The selected task
  object doubles as the "is this modal open?" flag (editingTask && 
  <EditTaskModal>), so opening a modal and seeding its data is one setState.
  - Buttons disabled while in-flight prevent double-submit/double-delete.

  Requirements coverage

  - 10 per page — TASKS_PER_PAGE = 10 slices the list.
  - Navigation — Prev/Next and numbered page buttons; clicking page 2 shows
  tasks 11–20.
  - Dynamic to total — totalPages = ceil(tasks.length / 10); the control count
  adjusts automatically as tasks are added/removed.
  - No full reload — pure client-side state (page); changing pages just
  re-slices the array, no network call and no navigation.
  - Intuitive/responsive — active page highlighted, Prev disabled on page 1 /
  Next on the last page, page list wraps on narrow screens, and a "Showing X–Y
  of N" range indicator.

  How it behaves with the existing CRUD

  - Why client-side: GET /api/tasks returns the whole list (no server paging),
  and the dashboard already loads all tasks for the summary. Paginating the
  in-memory array keeps everything reactive with zero backend changes and no
  extra requests when switching pages.
  - Create → setPage(1) + reload; since the API orders by CreatedDate desc, the
  new task is at the top of page 1, so you immediately see it.
  - Delete → reload shrinks the list; usePagination clamps the page (e.g.
  deleting the last item on page 2 of 2 moves you back to page 1) so you're
  never stranded on an empty page.
  - Edit → reload keeps you on the current page.

  ▎ Note: only the current 10-row slice is passed to TaskTable; the summary 
  ▎ cards still reflect all tasks (they're computed from the summary endpoint, 
  ▎ independent of the visible page).

  To try it: with the API + npm run dev running, the seeded 12 tasks now show 10
  on page 1 and 2 on page 2, with working Prev/Next/number controls.

  If you'd later prefer true server-side pagination (scales to large datasets,
  GET /api/tasks?page=&pageSize= with a paged response), that's a backend
  addition — say the word and I'll design it across the API + repository + this
  hook.

● Builds clean — 103 modules. Task filtering is implemented.

  Files

  ┌─────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │            File             │                   Role                    │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ components/TaskFilters.jsx  │ Status + Priority dropdowns (All + the    │
  │ (new)                       │ enum options) and a contextual "Clear     │
  │                             │ filters" button.                          │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                             │ Accepts a filters object and passes it to │
  │ hooks/useDashboardData.js   │  getTasks(filters) → server-side          │
  │ (updated)                   │ filtering via GET                         │
  │                             │ /api/tasks?status=&priority=.             │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ pages/DashboardPage.jsx     │ Owns filter state, memoizes the filters   │
  │ (updated)                   │ object, resets to page 1 on change, and   │
  │                             │ keeps controls visible during refetch.    │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ index.css                   │ Filter bar styles.                        │
  └─────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Requirements coverage

  - Filter by status & priority — two dropdowns; options are To Do / In Progress
  / Done and Low / Medium / High / Critical (sourced from the enum maps).
  - Combine filters — both are sent together, so "Critical + In Progress" works
  (e.g. ?status=1&priority=3); the backend TaskFilterDto ANDs them.
  - Dynamic, no reload — changing a dropdown updates filters (memoized) → the
  hook refetches just the task list and re-renders. No full page reload.
  - Efficient queries — filtering is done by the API/database, not by filtering
  a client array (the backend applies WHERE on indexed Status/Priority).
  - Default = all — empty selects ('') produce an empty filters object → GET 
  /tasks with no params → all tasks.
  - Responsive & accessible — labeled <select>s, keyboard-native, wrap on narrow
  screens, disabled during in-flight fetches; consistent with the dashboard's
  existing field styling.

  UX details worth noting

  - Controls stay put while loading. Content now renders whenever summary exists
  (not gated on loading), so toggling a filter doesn't make the dashboard flash
  to "Loading…" — the filter bar/table stay visible and the controls just
  disable briefly during the refetch. The initial load still shows "Loading
  dashboard…".
  - Pagination resets to page 1 when filters change (so you don't land on an
  out-of-range page), and the "Showing X–Y of N" line + page count reflect the
  filtered result count.
  - Summary cards stay global. They keep showing all-task totals regardless of
  the active filter (the summary endpoint isn't filtered), so the colored cards
  remain a stable overview while the table narrows. If you'd prefer the cards to
  reflect the filtered set instead, that's a quick change — let me know.

  To try it: with API + npm run dev running, pick a Status and/or Priority — the
  table updates immediately; "Clear filters" returns to all tasks.

❯ Run Web API and React Together                                                
  Goal                                                                          
  Configure the solution so both the .NET Web API (dotnet run --project         
  src/TMS.API) and the React frontend (npm run dev) can run simultaneously from 
  VS Code.                                                                      
  Approach Options                                                              
  Use VS Code tasks.json to define two tasks:                                   
  Task 1: dotnet run --project src/TMS.API                                      
  Task 2: npm run dev (with cwd set to frontend)                                
  Create a compound task (run-all) that launches both tasks in parallel.        
  Alternatively, use the concurrently npm package to run both commands from a   
  single script.                                                                
  VS Code Tasks Setup                                                           
  Add a .vscode/tasks.json file in the solution folder.                         
  Define:                                                                       
  Task 1: Run Web API → dotnet run --project src/TMS.API                        
  Task 2: Run React → npm run dev (cwd = frontend)                              
  Compound Task: run-all → depends on both tasks, runs them in parallel.        
  Concurrently Setup (optional)                                                 
  Install: npm install concurrently --save-dev                                  
  In frontend/package.json, add script:                                         
  json                                                                          
  "scripts": {                                                                  
    "dev:all": "concurrently \"dotnet run --project ../src/TMS.API\" \"npm run  
  dev\""                                                                        
  }                                                                             
  Run with: npm run dev:all

  concurrently script (alternative).

     48 packages are looking for funding

● concurrently@10 is installed and added to devDependencies. Both approaches are
  set up.

  What I added

  1. .vscode/tasks.json (primary — VS Code tasks):
  - Run Web API → dotnet run --project src/TMS.API (cwd = workspace root)
  - Run React → npm run dev (cwd = frontend)
  - run-all → compound task, dependsOn both with dependsOrder: "parallel" —
  launches them together, each in its own dedicated terminal panel. It's the
  default build task.

  2. frontend/package.json (optional — concurrently):
  "dev:all": "concurrently \"dotnet run --project ../src/TMS.API\" \"npm run 
  dev\""
  Plus concurrently installed as a devDependency.

  How to run

  VS Code tasks (recommended):
  - Ctrl+Shift+P → Tasks: Run Task → run-all (or just Ctrl+Shift+B since it's
  the default build task).
  - Two terminals open in parallel — one for the API, one for Vite. Each is a
  dedicated panel so logs stay separate.

  Concurrently (single command):
  cd frontend
  npm run dev:all
  Runs both from one terminal (interleaved output). Note the path is
  ../src/TMS.API because the script runs with frontend as the working directory.

  Notes

  - The tasks are marked isBackground: true since dev servers stay running; stop
  them by closing the terminals or Ctrl+C.
  - Ports stay as configured: API on the launch-profile port (you've been using
  5210), Vite on 5173. The SPA already points at http://localhost:5210/api via
  .env.development, and CORS allows :5173 — so they talk to each other out of
  the box.
  - If your API ever comes up on a different port than 5210, update
  frontend/.env.development (VITE_API_BASE_URL) and restart Vite.

  You can verify quickly: Ctrl+Shift+B, wait for "Now listening on… :5210" and
  Vite's "Local: http://localhost:5173", then log in with admin / Admin@123.

  Quick note on what happened earlier: run-all isn't a shell command — it's a VS

  VS Code: Ctrl+Shift+P → Tasks: Run Task → run-all (or Ctrl+Shift+B). If you'd
  rather start both from a terminal, use cd frontend && npm run dev:all (the
  concurrently script).
